# Blood Craft

**Book One of the Blood Craft Series**

---

# **Chapter 1**

The full moon hung low in the night sky, a luminous orb casting a silvery glow over the darkened landscape as my parents
and I cruised down the winding two-lane road late at night. There was something oddly enchanting about its
presence—tonight especially, it seemed closer somehow, more intimate, as though it were following our journey with
ancient, knowing eyes. I could have sworn it radiated a warm, reddish hue that filled me with an inexplicable sense of
comfort, a feeling that seemed to seep into my very bones. Ever since I can remember, I have been captivated by the
mysteries of the night, finding solace in its quiet embrace. I preferred the intimate darkness to those early risers'
overwhelming brightness and vitality, with their cheery dispositions and sun-kissed smiles.

On countless evenings, I found myself alone in the woods that bordered our property, wandering among the towering trees.
The gentle rustle of the leaves and the sound of critters busying themselves with their nightly routines enchanted me,
painting a vivid picture of life that thrived in the shadows. Fireflies would dance between the branches like earthbound
stars, and the distant hooting of owls served as my companions through the darkness. While I wouldn't strictly label
myself as an outdoorsy person, there was an undeniable allure to the night that soothed my restless spirit and piqued my
curiosity about nature's secrets—secrets that, as I would soon discover, ran far deeper than I ever imagined.

My mother often chastises me for my penchant for moonlit adventures, labeling me a night owl, a title I share with my
father. He often reassures me with an amused chuckle, "It's in our blood; we can't help that we are creatures of the
night." The way he said it—with that particular emphasis on 'blood'—always struck me as odd, though I never questioned
it. In these moments, my mother would playfully jest about living in a household filled with vampires, suggesting that
perhaps we should invest in a set of coffins. Her humor added fun to our quirks, reminding me that even in our oddity,
family bonds were cherished. Little did I know how prophetic her words would prove to be.

To characterize my family as movie buffs would barely begin to describe our cinematic obsession. On weeks where life
permits, we indulge in at least three to six films, drawing a variety of stories into our living room. My mother and I
share an undeniable passion for horror films, particularly those that revel in grotesque gore and thrilling violence.
There’s something exciting about immersing ourselves in the eerie and the macabre. However, I carry a secret: my heart
flutters for romantic comedies and tales of love that tug at the heartstrings. I’d never dare confess this to my father,
who is quite set in his ways. Some of my all-time favorite movies include “Tombstone,” “The Ugly Truth,” “The Proposal,”
“Phantom of the Opera,” “Queen of the Damned,” “Fight Club,” and “Lord of the Rings.” The list stretches on endlessly,
but these films resonate deeply and never fail to draw me in whenever I watch them.

As for Dad, he holds a different cinematic compass, gravitating towards mind-bending sci-fi and adrenaline-pumping
action films. His enthusiasm for intergalactic travels and explosive adventures brings a contrasting dynamic to our
family’s movie nights, often resulting in lively debates about the merits of each genre. In the end, whether exploring a
horror film's eerie darkness or romance's warm embrace, movie night always solidifies our connection, binding us in
shared experiences and laughter.

My parents dedicated the last 25 years of their lives to a quaint little town known as West, Texas. Nestled between the
bustling cities of Dallas and Waco, West is home to approximately 3,000 residents. The town boasts a rich and
captivating history; it was established in the mid-1800s when several farming families settled there after purchasing
land from the government. Over the years, West transformed into a thriving community, especially following the
construction of a significant railroad that linked it to an extensive rail network traversing Texas, Oklahoma, Kansas,
and Missouri. This connectivity opened the floodgates for new opportunities, leading to an influx of Czech immigrants in
the late 1800s. They arrived with dreams of a prosperous future, purchasing the region's fertile land to cultivate a new
life in America. By the early 1900s, it was evident that the town's demographic had shifted, with a majority of its
inhabitants proudly tracing their roots back to Czech ancestry, as evidenced by their distinctive, often challenging
last names.

One of the town's most cherished traditions is Westfest, a vibrant celebration held every year during Labor Day weekend.
This event pays homage to the area's rich Czech heritage and is a highlight for both locals and visitors. The festival
fills the air with lively entertainment, featuring authentic Czech music that resonates through the streets,
mouthwatering traditional foods that tantalize the taste buds, and an abundance of family-oriented activities that
foster community spirit and togetherness.

My parents attended Westfest one year, and the experience was instrumental in solidifying their decision to move to the
area. They found the residents to be welcoming and amiable, and they appreciated the close-knit nature of the community.
While the people of West cherish their traditions and values, they are also open to newcomers, as long as those
newcomers contribute positively to the community and respect its long-established way of life. This sense of belonging
and acceptance played a significant role in my parents’ love for their new home.

After achieving financial stability and seeking a change of pace, my parents made the significant decision to relocate
from Dallas to the quieter area of West, TX, several years prior to my birth, specifically in the vibrant decade of the
1990s. They envisioned a lifestyle that embraced tranquility, and so they purchased a tract of land just a few miles
outside of town where they built a charming house infused with their personal touches and a sense of warmth.

My father, a dedicated computer programmer, primarily worked from the comfort of our home, only venturing back to Dallas
for essential meetings and project collaborations. This arrangement not only allowed him to balance work and family life
but also fostered an environment rich in technology and innovation around me. Meanwhile, my mother took on the vital
role of managing our household. She decided to homeschool me, believing that the conventional education system did not
align with their values and aspirations for my growth. Although I didn't mind being homeschooled, I did feel the absence
of regular social interactions with peers, which meant I had fewer real friends growing up.

However, I found companionship in my passion for computer gaming, which served as a bridge to connect with others who
shared similar interests online. The remarkable internet connection my dad ensured we had—even in our remote countryside
setting—opened up a world of online communities and gaming experiences. My enthusiasm for technology reached new heights
when, at the age of ten, I built my first computer. It was a thrilling experience that ignited a deep-seated passion for
understanding the mechanisms of technology.

This fascination ultimately led me to pursue a degree in Computer Science, a field that mirrored my interests and
strengths. I am currently on track to complete my degree at the end of the upcoming semester, although the journey has
taken me longer than the typical timeline. After earning my high school diploma, I chose to take a break from formal
education. This time allowed me to help my parents with the upkeep of our home and the expansive land we had, while also
cherishing precious moments spent with them. This decision to pause my studies was not made lightly but stemmed from a
desire to strengthen our family bonds before diving back into my educational pursuits.

As we navigated the serpentine road, flanked by tall trees whose leaves danced in the gentle breeze, I found my mind
wandering to the significant transformations in my life, particularly in the realm of my social interactions. Since
starting college, my once lonely existence had blossomed into a lively tapestry of friendships and connections, making
me wonder why I had hesitated for so long to embark on this journey. Before this change, my experiences with women were
almost non-existent, leaving me with a hollow sense of longing that I now felt was finally being filled.  I soon
realized that my sexual desires leaned far from the typical “vanilla” flavors most people gravitate toward. Instead,
they gravitated toward the deeper, more complex shades of kink. This awakening happened in the intimate glow of the
bedroom, where I discovered not only my own preferences but also the thrill of my dominant personality. Each interaction
unveiled layers of my desires I hadn’t fully explored before, drawing me into a world of passion and power play that
felt exhilaratingly right.  After exploring the intricacies of relationships through a series of casual late-night
encounters with intriguing yet questionable individuals and in a variety of unconventional places, I found myself
yearning for a deeper understanding of both my own identity and the world around me. This desire to gain insight led me
to delve into the complexities of BDSM, a community that intrigued me with its blend of sensuality, trust, and power
dynamics. Eager to learn more, I began to immerse myself in books, articles, and discussions, seeking to comprehend the
psychological and emotional aspects of these practices, as well as the rich history and diverse lifestyles within the
BDSM culture. Through this journey of discovery, I hoped to gain clarity about my own desires and boundaries while
fostering a greater appreciation for the nuances of human relationships.

After dedicating time to thorough research, I came across various local communities that are passionately committed to
embracing unique identities and interests. These groups serve as safe havens where like-minded individuals gather to
express themselves freely, without the threat of judgment or ridicule that often comes with exploring unconventional
passions.

As I delved deeper into this vibrant subculture, I realized that I had developed a profound fascination with the dynamic
of submissive women, particularly those who take on the playful and alluring traits associated with feline
creatures—commonly known as Cat Girls. This particular aesthetic captured my imagination, combining elements of whimsy,
grace, and an enchanting sense of vulnerability that I found irresistible.

The more time I spent in these communities, the more my interest grew into a gentle obsession, pulling me into a world
rich with creativity and personal expression, where the boundaries of identity and fantasy intertwine beautifully.

I quickly reminded myself to stay focused and not let my mind drift into the myriad of delightful pains and pleasures
that linger in that particular headspace. It was a tempting territory, full of memories and fantasies, but I was
currently stuck with my parents in the cramped confines of our car. The familiar scent of the upholstery mixed with the
soft hum of the engine was grounding, yet my thoughts were eager to escape. I shook my head vigorously, trying to dispel
the swirling thoughts that plagued my mind, and redirected my focus to the captivating rural landscape outside my
window. The night unfurled like a dark velvet blanket, dotted with twinkling stars illuminating the fields' contours and
distant hills. Shadows danced across the terrain, shifting with the gentle breeze that rustled the leaves in the trees.
Each passing moment revealed new shapes and colors as the moon cast a silvery reddish glow over the meandering roads and
patches of farmland, beckoning me to lose myself in the serene beauty of the night.

As we drove through the winding roads, a sense of anticipation filled the air. We were embarking on a weekend getaway, a
refreshing break from our usually quiet, home-bound lifestyle. This trip held a unique significance for my family; it
was my birthday wish for this year. My 23rd birthday loomed on the horizon, set for October 31st, just four days away. I
felt a bubbling excitement, my thoughts racing with all the possibilities. Being born on Halloween had always had its
perks—an endless supply of treats, playful costume parties, and the thrill of spooky celebrations. However, this time
around, I craved something different—a respite from the chaos of social gatherings. What I envisioned instead was an
escape deep into the embrace of nature, a tranquil weekend spent enjoying the wilderness alongside my parents.

It became increasingly clear over the years that my parents were not particularly fond of socializing; they were
quintessential introverts. They never exhibited any overt rudeness toward others, nor were they socially awkward, but
their body language often betrayed their discomfort in social settings. A subtle shrug or an uneasy smile spoke volumes
about their preference for solitude. They seemed perfectly happy in each other's company, thriving in their own little
world without the need for a broader social circle. Dad initially showed a flicker of hesitation about leaving our cozy
home for the unknown, but Mom, ever the optimistic force, championed the idea, assuring him that it would be a fantastic
bonding experience. After some light-hearted back-and-forth, he finally relented.

They had rented a charming cabin nestled in the heart of Broken Bow, Oklahoma. From my research on social media, it
seemed like a hidden gem—one that promised a wealth of outdoor activities in a breathtaking national park setting.
Broken Bow Lake, in particular, stood out in the pictures I scrolled through, a vast expanse of crystal-clear water
cradled by emerald woods and rugged mountains. It was the perfect backdrop for a peaceful getaway.

Suddenly, the vibrating alert on my phone jolted me from my reverie. I glanced at the screen, my curiosity piqued by the
unrecognized number flashing back at me. The 254 area code was local—familiar—yet something about seeing it made my skin
prickle with unease. In the front seat, I noticed my parents exchange a quick glance, their bodies stiffening almost
imperceptibly. With a playful smirk, I decided to answer it, driven by spontaneity and a hint of mischief, pushing aside
the strange feeling settling in my stomach.

“Good Evening, Riven Sixxx speaking. How may I help you, Mate?” I said, slipping into my best British accent, which I
always used for unknown callers. There was a pause on the other end—a stillness so profound that it felt like the world
had come to a halt. And then, just like that, the line went dead, leaving me hanging in bemusement.

Dad burst into a hearty laugh, the sound resonating through the car as he playfully slapped the steering wheel with his
palm. Mom couldn’t resist joining in, a smile breaking out on her face as she rolled her eyes indulgently. “Another spam
caller, I take it?” she suggested with a smirk.

“I have no clue! They didn’t say a word and just hung up,” I replied, shrugging. “But hey, the 254 area code might have
belonged to someone we know. Can’t blame me for having a bit of fun, right, Dad?”

He chuckled, slightly hesitant, and replied, "Of course not, I…" But then he caught one of Mom's pointed looks—a look
I'd seen them exchange before, though I'd never understood its meaning—and his tone shifted. "However," he continued,
emphasizing the words as if to drive home an important point, "we all agreed this would be a tech-free weekend." His
gaze flicked to me, playful yet serious, and there was something behind his eyes—worry? fear?—before he shot me a cheeky
wink once Mom's attention wandered.

“Where are we now?” I asked, peering out the window as the trees closed in around us, shrouded in shadows, while the
night sky blossomed with stars—a dazzling tapestry of light that seemed infinitely deeper than I was used to. The moon
cast its soft glow across the landscape, illuminating our path.

“We’re about an hour from the cabin,” Dad replied, his voice filled with a hint of excitement as he turned down the
radio, which was serenading us with Frank Sinatra’s smooth vocals.

After a brief moment of silence, he turned back to me, inquisitive. “Once we get there and unpack, are you planning to
go to sleep right away, or are you going to stay up for a bit?”

I tapped my finger against my lips, pretending to contemplate the question, and after a brief pause, I answered, “I
think I want to explore the area. The night sky will be spectacular out here, free from city lights. You can really see
the stars shining clearer than ever.” My heart raced at the thought of stargazing in the great outdoors—a fitting way to
celebrate my upcoming birthday, away from the usual noise and bustle of life.

With a glimmer of hope in her eyes, my mother turned to me and softly pleaded, “Could I join you on this walk? It sounds
absolutely delightful, especially after enduring three long hours of Sinatra’s crooning during the drive.” She gestured
with her hands, sweeping them wide from her head as if to express just how overwhelmed she felt, her arms rising like
they were trying to embrace the very joy she sought.

I burst into laughter, nearly snorting as I playfully replied, "I wouldn't mind that at all, Mom. Dad can start cooking
on the grill as a fitting punishment for his stubborn choice of music on the way here.”

With a mischievous grin spreading across his face, Dad leaned back in his seat, launching into his best—and absolutely
terrible—imitation of the character Dean Winchester from his beloved show, Supernatural. “Driver picks the music, and
shotgun shuts their cake hole,” he declared in a deep, dramatic voice that caused us all to erupt in laughter.

The warmth of the moment wrapped around us like a cozy blanket, the shared humor creating a bond that made the journey
feel even more enjoyable. We chuckled together for what felt like a solid minute, the sound of our laughter mingling
with the rustle of the trees outside the car windows. Eventually, the music faded back into the background, but the joy
lingered. As we continued on our way to the cabin, a peaceful and happy silence enveloped us, filled with the subtle hum
of the road and the promise of the relaxing weekend ahead. None of us noticed the darkness that seemed to gather at the
edge of the headlights, nor the way the moon above us had begun to shift from silver to crimson.

# **Chapter 2**

It couldn't have been more than 15 minutes after the music cut off abruptly, silencing the cheerful notes that filled
the air and causing my head to snap up in alarm. The silence was deafening—not just the absence of music, but something
deeper, as if the world itself had drawn a breath and held it. I glanced at my parents, their faces pale and taut in the
dashboard's glow. They exchanged a look charged with unspoken words, a fleeting glimpse of fear and urgency that I had
never seen before. In hushed tones, they began to mumble to each other, their voices edged with anxiety, but I strained
to hear anything that could decipher this unsettling moment. It almost sounded like Dad muttered something about "they
found us," but surely that couldn't be right. My imagination was playing tricks on me—what possible reason would he have
to say that?

“How could they even know where we are at this hour?” Mom's voice quivered with a nervous intensity that pulled my
attention away from my swirling thoughts.

“They were most likely the ones on the other end of the phone call Riven got earlier,” Dad responded, his tone grave and
full of foreboding.

Without warning, we were plunged into an impenetrable darkness as though a vast, heavy curtain had been drawn across the
sky, swallowing the night whole. The temperature in the car plummeted, and I could see my breath misting in the sudden
cold. Then came a sound—a deep, grinding rumble that seemed to come from the earth itself. Suddenly, there was a
deafening thud as something collided violently with the car, jerking us from our path, the tires momentarily losing
their grip on the asphalt. A frisson of fear raced down my spine, and the hair on the back of my neck and arms stood on
end, my senses heightening in response to the jolt that surged through the vehicle and into my very core. The smell of
ozone filled the air, sharp and electric, mixing with something else—something ancient and earthen.

My parents' faces contorted in a mosaic of emotions—anxious glances, furrowed brows, and shadows of guilt intertwined
with palpable fear. In that moment, I saw them differently than I ever had before: not as the protective parents who had
sheltered me all my life, but as people carrying secrets too heavy to bear. The realization hit me like a physical blow,
stealing the breath from my lungs. Every childhood memory suddenly shifted, took on new meaning—all those times Dad called
us "creatures of the night," Mom's jokes about vampires, their carefully controlled lives in isolation. Had I ever truly
known them at all?

Then, my mother turned to me with an intensity so profound it sent chills coursing through me. Her eyes—had they always
been that shade of amber, liquid gold catching the strange light, or was this the first time I was truly seeing her?—
glistened with unshed tears that tracked silver down her cheeks. She reached back, her hand finding mine, squeezing with a
desperate strength that bordered on pain. "No matter what happens, know we love you and did our best to protect you from
what is coming," she declared, her voice steady yet laced with urgency, with finality. The words settled over me like a
shroud, heavy with goodbye.

"Mom, what are you talking about?" The words came out strangled, my throat constricting around them. A whirlwind of panic
spiraled within me, drowning rational thought. "You're scaring me! What the fuck is going on? What is coming and why? How
does a random spam call connect to any of this?" I found myself shouting, desperation rising in my tone, overwhelmed by
confusion. My hands shook, fingers digging into the leather seat. The normal rules of my world felt shattered, especially
when my parents didn't even flinch at my frantic exclamations—as if they'd been expecting my terror, preparing for this
moment my entire life.

My mind raced, a cacophony of questions spiraling like a tornado, each one fragmenting into more questions, more doubts,
more fear. The familiar interior of our car suddenly felt alien, as if I'd woken into a stranger's nightmare. My
heartbeat pounded in my ears, a frantic drum against my ribs. Just then, my watch emitted a series of sharp beeps,
pulling my attention to its glowing face. Alarmingly, the heartbeat sensor indicated my pulse was soaring beyond its
normal range—165, 170, climbing.  Before I could fully
grasp what was happening, I was shaken by a roaring sound that mixed with an unsettling rumble as the car lurched
skyward, airborne as if caught in a cyclone. In an instant, my body was thrust against the roof, and everything faded
into an abyss of darkness.

As I slowly opened my eyes, consciousness seeped back into my mind, bringing with it a jarring realization: the interior
of the car was suffocated in a ghastly shade of red, covering nearly sixty percent of the space around me. A chilling
wave of freezing shock washed over me as I recognized it was blood. My blood? Their blood? I couldn't tell, and the
not-knowing was somehow worse than certainty. I strained to take in my environment, but everything remained a hazy blur,
as if I were gazing through a fogged-up window. The relentless, high-pitched ringing in my ears was an all-too-familiar
sound—a cruel echo of chaos that hung in the air like a ghost. Gradually, the sharp scent of gasoline invaded my
nostrils, its potent odor sharp and suffocating, adding to my disorientation. My heart raced as I fought to steady
myself, desperate to shake off the veil of shock clouding my thoughts. I became aware of my position: still crammed in
the backseat, which had now toppled onto its side, a position that felt unnatural and wrong. The vehicle appeared to be
far removed from the road, its former path obscured by darkness and debris.

Above me, a full red moon cast a strange glow, its eerie light washing over the scene with a surreal vibrancy that only
amplified my dismay. The surroundings were shrouded in an unsettling crimson hue, the world transformed into something
nightmarish. Time seemed to stand still as I battled the disorientation, piecing together the remnants of what had
happened and realizing the gravity of my situation.

	A soft yet urgent voice broke the tense silence from the front seat, pulling me out of my thoughts. 

“Riven, are you okay?” The concern in their tone was palpable, cutting through the stillness like a knife. I glanced at
the clock on the dashboard; time was slipping away faster than I realized. “Listen, I need you to grab something from
the glovebox. We don’t have much time.”

Stuttering in disbelief and fear, I managed to say, “I’m fine, Mom, but where's Dad?” My voice trembled as I scanned the
interior of the car, searching for familiar signs of comfort in a place that now felt foreign and terrifying. The
driver’s seat was empty, an unsettling absence hanging in the air. My heart raced as I noticed the windshield, which had
been shattered into a spiderweb of glass, glittering like shards of ice in the moonlight. The sight of my father’s door
was even more alarming; it looked as The Hulk had ripped it off its hinges, the metal crumpled and twisted beyond
recognition.

“Don't worry about that right now!” she barked, her voice booming with an authority that sent shivers down my spine—a
tone I had never heard from her before. There was a raw urgency in her command that cut through my confusion. “Do as I
asked and get to the glove box now!”

Her eyes were wide with panic, and I could see the tension in her shoulders, her knuckles white as they gripped the
edges of her seat. Not fully grasping why she couldn't reach the glove box herself, I began to carefully climb over the
seat, each utterly painful movement filled with a mix of apprehension and instinct. Then, as realization struck like a
bolt of lightning, I halted abruptly.

The terrifying truth dawned on me: my mother wasn't moving because she was pinned, unable to maneuver or escape the
destruction surrounding us. Massive, jagged spikes, seemingly forged from a blend of stone and earth, pierced through
her, pinning her against the car's interior with an insurmountable weight. They looked wrong—too precise, too deliberate
to be an accident of nature. 

"No." The word fell from my lips, barely a whisper. "No, no, no..." My mind refused to accept what my eyes were seeing.
This couldn't be real. Any second now, I'd wake up in the backseat, Mom would turn around and smile, tell me we were
almost there. But the metallic tang of blood filled my nostrils, mixing with the acrid smell of twisted metal and
something ancient—earth and stone that didn't belong here.

It was not alone; several other similar spikes protruded ominously throughout the dimly lit cabin and my mother's body,
each one a menacing reminder that this was no accident. This was murder. Deliberate. Planned. Someone had done this to
her—to us.

"Mom..." My voice cracked, a child's plea wrapped in an adult's throat.

I tried to shake the haunting image from my mind, even though I knew it would remain seared into my consciousness
forever—the way the moonlight caught the blood, the impossible angle of the spikes, the too-still stillness of her body.
My heart raced as I reached for the glove box, my fingers trembling violently. The mystery of what lay inside beckoned to
me through the fog of denial still clinging to my thoughts.

"In the back, a small metal case, inside there's a vial; please, grab it." Her voice was a faint whisper, laced
with pain and urgency—but also love, so much love it hurt worse than any physical wound. How was she still speaking? How
was she still here with me? I fumbled in the dark confines of the cramped vehicle, my heart racing as I sifted through
the chaos, desperate to find the vial. Each labored breath she took seemed to pull the air from my own lungs.

"Take the vial… and get out of the car. Find a woman named Raechelle; she will help you. Get away from here, go home,
and look for my journal. It will explain everything." Her voice faltered, growing weaker with each word, yet she
summoned the strength to continue. Every instruction felt like goodbye. "Remember to always trust the signs and listen to
your heart. The magic in your blood will guide you when nothing else can." 

Magic? Blood? None of this made sense, but I couldn't ask, couldn't interrupt, because somewhere deep inside I knew—this
was the last time I'd hear her voice.

A single tear traced down her cheek, leaving a glistening trail through the dust and blood on her face. "I love you,
Riven. More than you'll ever know. Make us proud." Her gaze bore into mine, a mixture of desperation and resignation, as
if she was trying to memorize my face one final time, to carry it with her wherever she was going. The intensity of that
look felt like a brand on my soul.

I could feel tears stinging my eyes, hot and immediate, as I finally wrapped my trembling fingers around the cool metal
of the case. "Mom, I can't—please don't—" I opened my mouth to beg, to bargain, to promise anything if she'd just stay,
but the moment my eyes locked onto hers, I was met with something that shattered me completely.

Her eyes were distant now, looking through me rather than at me. The light that had always been there—the warmth, the
recognition, the unconditional love—was fading like stars at dawn. I watched it slip away, second by agonizing second,
and there was nothing I could do to stop it. The chilling emptiness that crept into her gaze signaled she was slipping
away from me, and the world tilted on its axis.

"No! Mom! MOM!" The scream tore from my throat, raw and primal. This wasn't happening. This couldn't be happening.

A wave of dread surged through my chest, and I was engulfed by the increasingly acrid scent of cheap unleaded fuel that
permeated the air. Panic coursed through me, urging me to act and scramble out of the soon-to-be death trap. I had to
get Mom out. I made a frantic move to retrace my steps back into the car, but before I could reach her, a powerful grip
seized me from behind, wrenching me away and hurling me backward.  The ground rushed up to meet me with a brutal thud,
the impact knocking the breath from my lungs and sending a jolt of pain through my body. Everything around me seemed to
explode as the vehicle erupted in a fiery conflagration, the flames licking upward and consuming the wreckage. The blast
was thunderous, shaking the earth beneath me and sending vibrant orange light cascading through the trees, disorienting
me further.

As I struggled to regain my footing, disoriented and gasping for air, I caught sight of a dark figure looming nearby.
Dressed in a shadowy hoodie that concealed their face, the figure was the one who had knocked me down, and an
instinctual fear coursed through me. My heart raced as I gathered my thoughts, ready to confront whoever it was that had
suddenly inserted themselves into my already tumultuous reality.

Tears streamed down my face as I screamed at the figure emerging from the shadows. "You fucking asshole! My mom was
still in the car," I shouted, my voice cracking with a mixture of rage and despair. The words hung in the air, heavy and
suffocating, like a weight pressing down on my chest.

The figure's response was unsettlingly calm, almost devoid of emotion, yet beneath that composure I sensed something
ancient, something that had seen centuries of death and learned to compartmentalize it. She stepped closer to me, her
features hidden even by the moonlight, moving with a fluid grace that was somehow both predatory and protective. Her
eyes were the only visible element, slightly glowing with an unnatural red hue that should have terrified me—yet
instead, they stirred something deep in my memory, a recognition I couldn't place. Her expression blank but for a hint
of sorrow flickering in them. "She was already dead," she stated flatly, her voice echoing in the silence that enveloped
us, carrying the weight of someone who had delivered such news too many times before. "I could hear her heartbeat no
more." A sense of hopelessness washed over me at her words, but also something else—a strange, inexplicable comfort in
her presence.

She continued, her voice low and grave, "As for your father, he fought valiantly, but in the end, he succumbed to their
relentless attack." The image of my father's fierce determination flashed through my mind, now forever silenced. "We are
alone," she said, her tone heavy with grief. "And if I hadn't pulled you away from the car, you would have died for
nothing."

Her words hit me like a punch to the gut. Despite my anger towards her, I couldn't deny the truth in what she was
saying. We were all that was left now. The weight of our survival rested on our shoulders alone.

"Believe this or not," she continued, her gaze meeting mine with intensity. "But I am not your enemy here." And in that
moment, as I looked into her eyes and saw the pain and loss mirrored there, I knew she was telling the truth. We were on
the same side, fighting against a common enemy that had taken everything from us.

Panic surged through me as I felt the small case I was still clutching tightly in my hand. "Who are you?" I demanded, a
cautious edge creeping into my voice as the reality of the situation began to sink in. “Do you know what this vial is
that she made me get out of the glovebox?” The realization that the voice addressing me was undeniably feminine did
little to ease the weight of dread settling in my chest.

Her gaze bore into me, and she leaned closer, her interest piqued. "What did she tell you?" The question purred from her
lips, laden with a curiosity that sent chills down my spine.

each pull of the drawer filled with the scent of lavender and old fabric, my fingers brushing against forgotten garments
and trinkets. I meticulously explored every nook and cranny, hoping to stumble upon the journal—an essential key to
understanding the enigma that loomed larger with every passing moment.

After an hour of meticulously combing through the cluttered shelves and boxes in the dimly lit attic, I turned to
Raechelle with a sense of urgency. “Do you have any idea where the journal might be?” I asked, my voice laced with
frustration.

She tilted her head slightly, her lips pinching in thought. “What did your mother say about it?” Raechelle inquired, a
hint of curiosity in her tone.

Letting out a small sigh, I ran my fingers through my hair, trying to quell the growing frustration. “Nothing much,
really,” I replied, the exasperation creeping into my voice. “She just told me to trust the signs and listen to my
heart. But what does that even mean? I just want to find the journal!”

As I relayed the troublesome message my mother had shared with me, my gaze was inadvertently drawn to an intriguing
symbol etched onto the nightstand beside me. My breath caught in my throat—it was unmistakably the same ominous emblem
that had adorned the vial from which I had sipped just hours earlier. The sight of it here, in my parents' room, sent a
shiver down my spine. How long had they kept this secret from me? Compelled by curiosity and a desperate need for
answers, I stepped closer to the nightstand and traced the contours of the symbol with my fingertips, feeling the edges
of the design under my skin. The wood seemed to pulse with a faint warmth beneath my touch. Upon closer inspection, I
noticed that the center of the pentagram appeared slightly different from what I had first observed—raised, like a
button waiting to be pressed. A whisper of instinct urged me to press down on this unusual feature, so I complied. To my
surprise, a resounding click echoed in the otherwise quiet room, signaling a mechanism at work. The past I thought I
knew was about to shatter completely. With a gentle lift, the top of the nightstand rose ever so slightly, with a mix of
excitement and trepidation, I grasped the edge of the nightstand and lifted it, revealing a compartment that had long
remained concealed. In its depths lay a heavily worn leather-bound journal, its surface marred by years of use and
whispers of forgotten stories. What caught my attention immediately was the pentagram embossed on the cover distinct
from the one I had seen earlier, boasting five separate symbols, each intricately placed at the tips of the star's five
points.

Starting from the apex, the first symbol resembled a circle, cradling a small double helix in its center—a potential
marker of something biological, a hint of life intertwined within its design.  Moving in a clockwise direction, I noted
the second symbol: a stark upside-down triangle, sharply defined and commanding attention. Next, a right-side-up
triangle sat adjacent, creating an intriguing balance between the two. The bottom left symbol was another upside-down
triangle, this one distinguished by a horizontal line bisecting it, suggesting a deeper meaning or separation. Finally,
at the leftmost point of the star, a right-side-up triangle replicated the previous design but was likewise adorned with
a horizontal line, adding layers to the symbology woven throughout this mysterious tome. Each symbol felt heavy with
meaning as if holding secrets waiting to be revealed.

As I lifted the journal, my fingers continued to trace the intricate lines of the detailed pentagram etched into its
cover. The leather was soft with age, warm to the touch, as if the book itself held life within its pages. Nestled
beneath it, a thick envelope caught my eye, its texture sturdy and inviting. My heart raced as I saw a single word
written in my mother's elegant handwriting: Riven. The mere sight of her familiar script sent a wave of nostalgia
through me, stirring memories that felt both distant and immediate—her hand guiding mine as she taught me to write, the
notes she'd leave in my lunchbox, the birthday cards filled with her love. I had to blink back tears before I could
continue.

As I reached for the letter resting in the hidden compartment, I felt my grip falter, nearly letting the journal slip
from my hands.  To steady myself, I sank down onto the edge of the bed.  With a deep breath, I placed the journal—a
weathered tome filled with my thoughts and secrets—gently beside me.  As I focused on the letter, I noticed the
intricate wax seal that adorned its flap, marked with the same pentagram I was becoming familiar with.  I took a moment
to appreciate the artistry of the seal before I carefully pulled the letter free, the crack of the wax breaking echoing
softly in the quiet room.

*Dear Riven, *

*If this letter has found its way to you, it signifies a turning point—either the unfolding of events that I must now
share or perhaps the troubling arrival of those who seek the knowledge your father and I possess. Please remember,
within your heart, that you are deeply cherished, and it pains us to have placed this heavy burden upon your young
shoulders. Our desire for a semblance of normalcy in our lives with you was driven by love, and for this fleeting
moment of selfishness, we genuinely apologize.*

*As you read these words, I’m certain you’ve taken the blood vial, the key to unlocking the dormant magic within you,
and I trust you are beginning to feel the empowering rush of your newfound abilities. In time, you will discover just
how crucial and remarkable you are destined to become.*

*The power you will uncover is boundless and vast; however, to achieve greatness as a mage, it is essential to master
the fundamental concepts that underlie the art.  At the core of magical practice lies the sacred pentagram, composed
of the five prime magical disciplines: Blood, Water, Fire, Earth, and Air. Each of these elements represents a
distinct pathway of magical expression, rich with its own intricacies and potential.*

*Most practitioners in the realm of magic, whether mages or sorcerers, tend to dedicate themselves to a single
discipline. The most adept and powerful users within these categories bear the esteemed title of Archons, each
embodying the essence of their respective magic. Your lineage, belonging to the illustrious Sixxx household, aligns
with Blood Magic, marking you as the first Blood Mage and namely thus Archon to emerge in centuries. While this
lineage bestows incredible potential, it does not come without its drawbacks and dangers. You and Rae will need to
navigate these challenges carefully to fully grasp the implications of your heritage.*

*The other four magical disciplines are equally potent in their own way, with each Archon honing unique abilities tied
intricately to their craft. The Archons—representatives of their elements—form a council of magical Archons,
collectively known as The Archonis Council.  This council is not merely a governing body; it has historically wielded
tremendous influence over the magical realm.  In order to a councilmember you must challenge the seated member to a
duel and defeat them in combat.*

*In the last three hundred years, the members of the Archonis has become stagnant, with only four of five Archons
currently serving and those four have held their positions each for a century or more.  A horrific event in history
marked the end of the last Blood Archon, whose insatiable thirst for power posed a grave threat to both the magical
and mundane worlds. Their excessive manipulation of Blood Magic led to a catastrophic decision by the other Archons,
resulting in his demise. In the aftermath, fear reigned supreme, prompting a relentless hunt for anyone linked to the
Blood Magic bloodlines. This deep-seated anxiety about the return of a Blood Archon has forced your lineage into
hiding, leading your family to adopt a life off the grid, distanced from the broader magical community and your
destined path.*

*Reflecting on the annals of history, there was once a figure of incredible prowess known as the Prime Archon—an
enigmatic, nearly mythical being believed to possess mastery over all five disciplines, capable of manipulating time
and space. Tragically, the records detailing his existence and extraordinary feats have been largely lost or
annihilated over the centuries, particularly during the brutal purges targeting your bloodline and others like it.
Whispers and rumors suggest that the Blood Archon lineage may have traceable roots linked to this Prime Archon,
further deepening the mystique surrounding your heritage.*

*Indeed, fear is a potent weapon; it has the power to warp minds and compel individuals to commit unspeakable acts in
its name. The history of your lineage is fraught with trepidation and cautious hope, placing the weight of the world
on your shoulders as you embark on this journey of self-discovery and magical awakening.*

*I implore you to place your trust in Raechelle. She is not just a helper; she is an integral part of our family’s
tapestry, woven into our lives for ages. Bound to you as a familiar, she is a magical creature with deep connections
to our bloodline. Familiars like Rae are enchanting beings, often taking on the characteristics of various animals,
their forms and abilities reflecting the unique magic they serve. While many share traits of wolves, birds, or even
reptiles, Rae is a beautiful cat familiar, gracefully poised with her piercing eyes and sleek fur. Her loyalty knows
no bounds, and her devotion to you surpasses that of any creature you’ll ever encounter.  Lean on her wisdom, and
allow her to guide you on this extraordinary journey that awaits. You are never alone in this—Rae is here to stand by
your side, ready to help you navigate the magic and challenges ahead.*

*Something else you should know **about** Rae if you **haven't** discovered it already is, due to a rather unfortunate
and complicated series of events that unfolded many years ago, she has become a child of blood—a vampire, to put it
plainly. However, I encourage you to set aside any preconceived notions or stereotypes you might have about vampires
based on the countless movies and shows we've watched together over the years. She will educate you about her unique
world and the intricacies of her kind. She has a wealth of knowledge to share, not only about vampires but also about
other supernatural beings that inhabit her universe. If you open your mind and allow her to guide you, you’ll discover
insights and truths about her existence that go far beyond the myths and legends of popular culture.*

*It is absolutely crucial for you to understand that Rae is bound to you as your familiar. This bond is not merely a
passing connection; it is a profound and eternal link. To illustrate this, think of her as your Mary Jane, your
Gamora, your Juliet, your Belle, or your Rapunzel—essentially, she represents your everything. I can’t help but
chuckle at how much I know you will enjoy these movie references, as they encapsulate the essence of our shared
experiences.*

*However, I suspect she isn't yet aware of the depth of the bond you share. At this moment, she may feel a compelling
attraction toward you, but she won't truly understand why this is happening. It will likely confuse and frustrate her
immensely, as everything you do or say will ignite a fire within her, an urge she might instinctively want to resist.
Though she may not have conscious memories of the event from almost 15 years ago, a significant moment occurred when
you first crossed paths when you were a child—at that moment, a blood bond was forged between you.  The blood bond is
an extraordinary and powerful connection that exists between two magical beings, creating an attraction that is far
stronger than physical gravity. It’s important to remember that you do not get to choose who you become bonded with;
the intricacies of magic and its energies are as enigmatic as the bond itself. This connection transcends the limits
of time and space, and it remains a relatively uncharted territory in the realm of magic—much is still undiscovered.*

*Once you both recognize and accept this connection, it will establish itself in a way that makes the two of you
inseparable. When your father and I first came to understand this bond, we took decisive action to protect you
both. We separated you and cast a powerful spell to ensure that the memories of your bond would fade until the moment
you kissed, shielding you from the intensity of the energies you would naturally emit. The forces at play between you
are so strong that they would have been obvious to any being of higher power, thus the need for protection.*

*In essence, your journey together is one of profound discovery, and as the bond unfolds, things will become clearer.
You will navigate this magical connection, and as you do, you may find that the strength of your shared bond is unlike
anything you have ever experienced.*

*I understand that this may be overwhelming for you, my dear son, but I have complete faith that you will rise to
become one of the greatest Archons our world has ever seen. Throughout your life, you have demonstrated an incredible
ability to absorb knowledge quickly, and I am confident that your natural inclinations toward kindness, care, and
dedication will serve you well as you embark on this monumental journey. Remember, it’s crucial to listen to your
heart and trust your instincts; they will invariably guide you along the path that is meant for you, no matter the
challenges that arise.*

*To assist you in this transformative process, I have left behind a comprehensive journal that your father and I
meticulously compiled over the years. This journal is filled with invaluable insights about the other Archons, their
experiences, and wisdom gleaned from their journeys. Within its pages, you will also find extensive training material
and knowledge specifically designed to help you hone your magical abilities. My greatest hope is that this journal,
coupled with the guidance of Rae, will provide you with the foundation you need until you are ready to confront the
significant challenges that lie ahead.*

*Moreover, nestled alongside this letter and the journal is a special ring, crafted with love and purpose by your
father. This ring has the unique power to conceal your abilities from those who might seek to uncover them. It is
essential that you wear it at all times until you have gained sufficient training and confidence to reveal your true
self to the world. Embrace this journey, my son, and know that you are never alone—our love and guidance will always
be with you.*

*Remember Riven, *

*With Great Power Comes Great Responsibility! Hahaha, see what I did there? *

*Love, *

*Mom*

I read the letter several times, each pass revealing layers of meaning and emotion that tugged at my heart. 

The first time through, I could barely process the words—Blood Archon, familiar bonds, protection spells. It was too much,
too fast, too impossible. My eyes skimmed over sentences without absorbing them, seeking only the shape of Mom's
handwriting, proof that she had held this paper, that her hand had moved across it with love and intention.

The second time, reality began to settle in with crushing weight. This was real. Magic was real. The supernatural world
was real. And I was supposed to be some kind of powerful being called a Blood Archon. The absurdity of it warred with the
evidence—the attack, the spikes that had killed them, Raechelle's crimson eyes. Every instinct screamed that this
couldn't be true, but I'd seen too much to deny it anymore.

The third time through, grief overwhelmed everything else. This was Mom's last message to me. These were some of the final
words she'd taken the time to write down, knowing—knowing—that she might not survive to speak them herself. She'd been
preparing for this, trying to protect me even in death. "Our love and guidance will always be with you." But I wanted her
here, not just her love. I wanted to ask her questions, to hear her voice one more time, to tell her I wasn't ready for
any of this.

By the fourth reading, I started to notice the smaller details. The movie references—Mary Jane, Gamora, Belle,
Rapunzel—chosen specifically because she knew they would resonate with me. The way she called Raechelle "Rae," suggesting
an intimacy, a friendship I'd never known existed. The fact that Raechelle had been watching over me since childhood,
that we'd met before and some spell had made us both forget. My entire life had been carefully orchestrated without my
knowledge.

And then, at the very end: "With Great Power Comes Great Responsibility! Hahaha, see what I did there?"

A laugh burst out of me—loud, unexpected, edged with hysteria. It probably echoed off the walls like the cackle of a
madman. She'd quoted Spider-Man. In her final letter, explaining that I was some kind of supernatural heir with enormous
magical abilities, entrusting me to a vampire familiar I was apparently mystically bonded to, warning me about enemies and
destinies... she'd made a Spider-Man reference. Because she knew it would make me laugh. Because even facing death, even
preparing her son for an impossible future, she was still Mom.

"She quoted Spider-Man, of all things," I muttered to myself, a bittersweet smile tugging at my lips as I wiped away the
tears that had unexpectedly spilled from my eyes—when had I started crying? The absurdity of it all—a superhero quote
slipping into such a surreal moment—felt strangely comforting. It was so perfectly her that for a moment, I could almost
hear her laughing with me.

But the laughter faded quickly, leaving behind only the ache of loss. She was gone. Dad was gone. And I was here, holding
this letter, expected to somehow become what they'd believed I could be.
In the corner of the bedroom, Raechelle stood silently, her presence blending with the night as though they were one.
She watched me with concern etched on her face before she finally spoke up. “I am deeply sorry for the loss of your
parents,” she said, her voice soft yet steady. “They have always been incredibly kind to me, and I will miss them
greatly. They were some of the only people I could truly call friends.”

Her words wrapped around me like a warm embrace, and I could sense her genuine sorrow. There was a moment of silence
between us, heavy with shared grief and unsaid thoughts. Then she continued, her eyes searching mine, “Did your mother
mention anything about me? What else did she mention? If you dont mind me asking?”

I noted the subtle hint of sadness that laced her voice, a melancholic echo that seemed to linger in the air between us.
Her crimson eyes, bright yet edged with curiosity, scanned my face, searching for something unspoken. Despite the late
hour, the room was dimly lit, with only the pale moonlight filtering through the window, casting soft shadows that
danced across her form. The darkness around her seemed to cloak her further, her features obscured by the oversized,
baggy clothes that hung loosely from her frame.

As I studied her, a flurry of thoughts raced through my mind about how best to approach Rachelle. Should I reveal the
profound connection I just learned existed between us? Or would it be wiser to keep that revelation locked away for now,
especially since I still had no clear understanding of her identity? My mother’s words echoed in my mind—she had assured
me that I could trust this girl, but uncertainty gnawed at me.

After a few moments of contemplation, I opted to keep the nature of our bond to myself for the time being, waiting for
the right moment to unveil it. Instead, I chose to share the other, more tangible truths: “She mentioned that you are a
cat familiar, deeply entwined with my bloodline. And that you are, in fact, a child of blood—a vampire.”

As I spoke, a mix of excitement and trepidation surged within me. I was keenly aware of the impact my words might have
on her, uncertain about how she would react to my revelations. To my surprise, she simply nodded, her acknowledgment
serving as a quiet confirmation of what my mother had written. Encouraged by her response, I took a breath and
continued, eager to unravel the mystery that enveloped us both.

“She briefly explained the intricacies of magic, the various Archons, and the reasons behind my ignorance regarding
these matters. Her revelations felt like shards of glass piercing through the fog that had clouded my mind for so long.
Most startling of all, she informed me that I am the Blood Archon — a title that resonated deeply within me, though I
couldn’t fully grasp its weight. She also cautioned me about potential adverse side effects associated with my newfound
identity. As if that weren’t enough, she mentioned a ring, a small, seemingly innocuous artifact, that would shield me
from detection by others.”

After her mention of the ring, my gaze was drawn back into the hidden compartment where it lay nestled in the back
corner, catching the moonlight like a dark star.

I reached in, the cool metal of the ring contrasting against my warm fingers, and upon closer inspection, I realized it
appeared to be nothing more than a simple black band, devoid of embellishments or markings. It seemed impossible that
such an ordinary item could possess the power she described. Driven by a mix of curiosity and urgency, I slipped it onto
my middle finger. To my astonishment, it shrank and molded itself to fit snugly against my skin, a clear sign of the
enchantment woven into its very essence.

Raechelle inhaled sharply at that moment, triggering an instinctual jolt of anxiety within me. I turned to her, startled
by the small gasp that escaped her lips.

“What’s wrong?” I asked, my voice laced with concern.

“I can no longer sense your magic,” she replied, her eyes widening with a mixture of surprise and relief. “That’s a good
sign and will greatly benefit us moving forward. Now that the cat is out of the bag, so to speak.” A smirk danced on her
lips, and she let out a soft chuckle that broke the tension in the air. “But we can’t stay here, at least for a couple
of days, until things settle down. After the attack, there will be those who sensed the sudden surge of energy. We
should find a safe spot in case they come looking for us.”

She pointed toward the shadowy expanse outside. “Fortunately, my home isn’t far from here; in fact, we won’t even need
to leave the property. There, we can rest and regroup. I am utterly exhausted, and we need to have a thorough discussion
about everything that’s happened.”

Without wasting another moment, she urged, “Quickly, gather the journal and anything else you think you’ll need. We must
move swiftly.”

I nodded, urgency coursing through my veins, and started to gather some clothes, essentials, and the journal that held
mysteries of its own, a silent testament to the journey I was about to embark upon. As we stepped out of the house, I
felt the weight of the world on my shoulders, but also a flicker of hope ignited by the unknown possibilities that
awaited us.

# **Chapter 4**

As we stepped out of the house, a swirl of thoughts consumed me, particularly that cryptic comment she had made: "We
won't even need to leave the property." It echoed in my mind, raising a flurry of questions. Did she actually reside
somewhere on our land? How long had she been there, and how on earth had I missed the presence of an unfamiliar woman in
these woods? I had spent countless hours wandering through the dense undergrowth and towering trees, yet somehow this
creature—this vampire, this familiar—had lived here all along, watching over me from the shadows. The idea of a stranger
living among them both puzzled and unsettled me, but also stirred something else: a strange sense of comfort, as if I
had always known, on some subconscious level, that I was never truly alone.

We ventured deeper into the woods, the light struggling to pierce the thick canopy overhead. Shadows danced around us,
creating an almost surreal atmosphere as the night continued into neverending darkness. In the dim light, I spotted a
hammock I had strung up between two sturdy trees, a personal retreat I cherished whenever I sought solace in nature's
embrace. Gazing at it, I felt a sense of comfort wash over me, a reminder of peaceful moments I had enjoyed there. Yet,
as I stood lost in my reverie, I noticed her reaction; she seemed to catch my glance and, for a fleeting moment, a smirk
flickered across her lips.

My mind, however, was still flooded with the copious details from the letter I had read earlier. Each line was laced
with mystery, leaving me eager yet apprehensive about what lay ahead. Clutched tightly in my hands was the journal—the
one I couldn’t bear to part with since leaving the house. The pages brimmed with secrets waiting to be uncovered, and I
felt a thrilling anticipation to delve into its depths. What revelations awaited me among the scribbled notes and
forgotten memories?

“Just a little further,” she murmured softly, her voice barely above a whisper as we navigated through the thickening
foliage. Each step she took seemed effortless, and remarkably, she seemed to glide above the forest floor, making hardly
a sound.

In contrast, I sensed every distinct sound around us with surprising clarity—the rustle of leaves under the gentle
breeze, the distant call of a bird, and the occasional snap of twigs underfoot. Yet, it was curious that I could only
just manage to catch the faint echo of her footsteps as she moved forward. This made me wonder about the enhancements to
my senses. Had my hearing sharpened in tune with my sight? What other mysteries about my perception lay in wait for me
to discover?

After nearly thirty minutes of silent exploration through the dense undergrowth, we emerged into an expansive clearing
that starkly contrasted the compact trees surrounding it. I blinked in sudden realization, feeling an unsettling
combination of intrigue and confusion. How long had this place existed, hidden away from my eyes without my knowledge?

“Here we are, my humble little cabin!” Raechelle announced, her voice brightening with enthusiasm as she gestured
broadly around the clearing. A visible wave of relaxation washed over her hidden frame, as if she had shed a weight that
had been burdening her.

I surveyed the scene with a puzzled expression. “What cabin?” I exclaimed, my brow furrowing in confusion. All I saw was
an empty expanse of land, just a wide-open plot surrounded by the towering trees that loomed like silent sentinels. The
clearing felt as vast as half a football field, its openness striking in the dense woods.

Raechelle’s eyes sparkled with a mixture of mischief and joy. “I wasn’t sure if the spell worked or not since no one has
ever been here before,” she explained, laughter dancing in her voice. “But at least now I know it can hide my home even
from an Archon.” She tossed me a dazzling wink, a playful acknowledgment of my newly bestowed title. It was the first
display of genuine emotion I had witnessed from her since we met, and it illuminated her features with a sparkle of
happiness. I could sense how much this place meant to her, as if it were a piece of her very soul, and her elation was
contagious, urging me to share in her moment of triumph.

Then she took my hand, which caught me by surprise, and spoke aloud, her voice carrying a ceremonial weight that seemed
to make the very air tremble: "Sir Riven, as my honored guest, never avert your gaze from my home." As she grasped my
hand, a surge of warmth enveloped me, surprising me with its intensity—it felt like electricity dancing between our
palms, connecting us in ways I couldn't explain. Her voice, gentle yet commanding, flowed through the still air. Almost
instantly, a tingling sensation raced through my fingertips, creeping up my arm and settling in my chest, resonating
with something that had always been there, dormant, waiting. I blinked, and the world around me transformed vividly, the
veil of illusion lifting like morning fog before the sun.

Before me stood a quaint little cabin, its wooden walls exuding a rich warmth as smoke drifted melodiously from the
chimney, curling lazily into the black specked sky. It was a striking display of tranquility that seemed impossible
given all that had happened: the cabin nestled snugly in a serene landscape, the surroundings both welcoming and
enchanting. For a moment, I forgot about grief, forgot about revenge, forgot about the terrifying new world I'd been
thrust into. There was only this—beauty, peace, sanctuary. Above, the night sky stretched endlessly, a breathtaking dome
studded with twinkling stars more vivid than I'd ever seen them. An ominous red moon bathed the scene in an ethereal
glow, infusing the area with an otherworldly beauty that somehow defied its unnerving color. Even under its shadowy
light, a profound feeling of relaxation washed over me, making me feel safe and at home. I let out a long, slow sigh, my
senses awakening to the peace that pervaded the air, easing the tightness that had built within me throughout the long,
terrible day.

To the right of the cabin, approximately ten feet away, was an artfully manicured garden bursting with vibrant herbs and
blooming flowers, their colors vivid against the lush greenery. The fragrance of earth and petals wafted through the
air, a delightful symphony of scents that lulled my thoughts. Nestled in a cozy nook between two towering trees was a
stunning handcrafted wooden bench, its surface worn smooth by years of use, inviting anyone to take a moment and savor
the view. Further back, slightly hidden by the foliage, I spotted the weathered outline of a well, its presence a silent
witness to generations of stories and memories. From my vantage point, the entire scene felt as though it had been
plucked from a dream, one that even the great Bob Ross himself would struggle to capture in brushstrokes.

“It’s beautiful; I’ve never seen anything like it,” I murmured, captivated by the scene’s radiance that seemed to
pulsate with life.

“It always brings me peace, even after all this time,” she replied softly, a wistful note in her voice, her gaze
drifting as if reliving distant memories.

“How long have you lived here? How long has the cabin been here?” I found myself blurting out, my curiosity overwhelming
my caution.

“Well, it’s been just over a century now that I think about it… umm, yes, 103 years this past spring, if memory serves
me right," she clarified, her eyes lifting to an unseen point in the distance, as if she were sifting through the sands
of time to reclaim those fleeting moments, her weariness evident.

“Wait, so you’ve lived here that long? That means you were here before my parents ever purchased the land! How is that
even possible?” The seriousness in my tone took me off guard, a mix of curiosity and bewilderment threading through my
words.

“Let’s go inside, please,” she urged, her tone softening but revealing a hint of urgency. “I need to change out of these
filthy clothes and find some comfort before we delve into everything. I promise, Sir, I will answer all your questions
after we’ve eaten and rested.”

Too weary to argue, I nodded, the lure of warmth and sustenance pulling me forward. Together we stepped inside the
cabin, and I was struck by its inviting atmosphere. A beautiful wood interior wrapped us in a rustic embrace, exuding a
feeling of age-old comfort, as if the very walls held countless shared moments. The living room boasted a plush black
sectional sofa, perfectly arranged to face the fireplace at its center, its brick mantel sturdy and adorned with a few
personal trinkets that told silent stories.

I scanned the room further, noticing its unpretentious simplicity; there were no electric lights to mar the cozy
ambiance, and no modern kitchen appliances to be seen—only a solid cast-iron kettle resting regally on the mantle, a
hint that this cabin operated by the old ways. Raechelle began lighting a handful of candles, their flames flickering to
life, casting a warm golden glow that danced across the walls as she started a fire in the hearth, the first crackling
sounds of burning wood filling the room with both sound and warmth.

As I absorbed the space, I noticed that there were only two other rooms. A bedroom revealed itself through an open
archway, and I caught sight of a beautifully crafted four-poster bed draped in soft, inviting linens, exuding an air of
serenity and restfulness. The other room, discreetly closed off by a sturdy door, must have been the bathroom.

As the need to relieve myself suddenly became apparent, I turned to Raechelle, pointing toward the closed door and
inquiring politely, “May I use your facilities?” My voice barely above a whisper, I felt an undeniable urge to blend
into this warm, welcoming sanctuary.

“Of course, please make yourself at home, Sir,” Raechelle replied, her voice laced with a playful tone that sent a
ripple of unexpected emotions through me. The way she addressed me stirred a mix of feelings I wasn’t quite prepared to
confront. Was she using “Sir” out of respect, or was there something more intimate behind her choice of words? I found
myself grappling with the implications of it, as that particular name had always been my preference in sessions with
submissives. Each time the title danced on her lips, it sent a little thrill coursing through me—one that I desperately
hoped she hadn’t noticed.

Stepping into the bathroom, I braced myself for whatever rustic surprises awaited me in this secluded cabin. The first
thing that caught my eye was an exquisite giant copper clawfoot tub, gleaming softly despite the lack of modern
amenities like a shower curtain. It was both beautiful and peculiar, a perfect embodiment of the cabin’s charm and its
eccentricities. I chuckled to myself, realizing that with no visitors in what felt like a century, the need for privacy
likely hadn’t been a concern for anyone.

movement a testament to her grace. My heart raced as I watched the bushy black tail deftly peek out from the hem of her
silky shorts, its glossy sheen glistening in the light. I felt a surge of admiration for her, sensing she was fully
aware of the effect her beauty had on me.

With a fluid motion, she turned, allowing me to take in the full scope of her magnificence. Sharp black claws peeked out
from beneath her fingers and toes, adding an element of fierce allure to her captivating presence. It was as if she was
a creature from a dream, combining elegance with an undeniable wildness.

After circling back to her original position, she reached for the necklace, intending to put it back on. I couldn’t
contain myself any longer.

“Please, for the love of all the blood in the world, don’t put it back on,” I pleaded, my voice rising with intensity.
“I honestly didn’t think you could become any more beautiful or perfect than you already are. Holy mother fucking shit,
was I wrong!” The words escaped my mouth in a fervent proclamation, fueled by awe and appreciation.

Startled at first by my unexpected outburst, her eyes widened in surprise. But as my words settled in, a grin
slowly spread across her face, and she began to relax, her giggles bubbling up like a sweet melody. “You think I look
perfect and beautiful? You actually want me to stay like this?” she asked, a playful sparkle dancing in her eyes.

With sincerity in my voice, I replied, “Absolutely! You are the embodiment of everything I have ever fantasized
about—the woman I have dreamt of claiming as my own since I first grasped the concept. If it were entirely up to me, you
would remain like this, radiating that perfect beauty 24/7. Yet, I completely understand why that can’t be our reality.
But, I need you to promise me something: when it’s just us, you’ll embrace this side of yourself.” My words tumbled out,
my heart racing as I struggled to express the depth of my feelings, still incredulous that this moment was real.

Her eyes sparkled with excitement as she squealed, “Yes, Sir! I promise I will be like this as often as I can for you.”
Her enthusiasm was infectious, and I couldn’t help but smile at her delight.

Then, I felt the gravity of the moment press upon me. I took a deep breath, steeling myself for what I was about to say.
“Then I have one very serious, life-altering question to ask you.” I stood before her, bowing slightly to emphasize the
significance of the moment. Maintaining eye contact, I extended my hand as if offering her a treasure, and I asked the
most important question of the night:

“Will you do me the honor of becoming Mine, Kitten?”

Faster than my eyes could perceive her movements, Raechelle took my hand and exclaimed, "Yes Sir, I will!" Her voice
rang with excitement as she jumped into the air, wrapping her legs around my waist with an electrifying energy that sent
my heart racing. The moment she secured her embrace, her eyes sparkled with pure joy, illuminating the room with her
happiness—centuries of loneliness melting away in a single word. As her lips brushed against mine, I felt an
overwhelming rush of passion; time seemed to stand still during the most breathtaking kiss of my life. Through the
nascent bond between us, I felt her emotions pouring into me: relief, joy, love so profound it made my chest ache, and a
possessive devotion that matched my own. Her tail swished playfully behind her, adding to the enchanting atmosphere
between us. In that moment, I understood why my mother had called her my Mary Jane, my Gamora, my everything. This was
fate, destiny, a connection that transcended time and death.

Once our embrace ended, we settled back down on the plush sofa, our laughter filling the cozy room. The warmth of the
fire crackled softly, creating an intimate ambiance as we entered a state of blissful giddiness. We spent the next few
hours engrossed in conversation, taking turns asking questions that ventured into a plethora of topics, each exchange
deepening our understanding of one another. I was captivated by her stories about the magical kingdom she hailed from,
filled with fantastical creatures, mystical landscapes, and intriguing laws that governed her world.  For example,
Arcane illusion spells wield immense power, capable of shrouding entire realms in layers of enchantment that distort
perception and reality. These spells have been crucial in keeping the magical world concealed from the ordinary eyes of
society, creating a veil that separates the mundane from the mystical. Similarly, social media plays a significant role
in this concealment; with its carefully curated images and narratives, it can manipulate public perception, leading
people to overlook or dismiss the extraordinary happenings that unfold in remote corners of the world. Strikingly, both
arcane magic and digital platforms thrive on the same principle: the art of illusion, enabling the hidden aspects of the
magical world to remain primarily unseen while bustling with life and wonder in secluded locations where the
extraordinary continues to flourish.

In turn, I opened up about my life over the past twenty years—the challenges I faced growing up without any knowledge of
magic, the loneliness that sometimes enveloped me, and the struggles I endured. Raechelle listened intently, her
expression shifting between sympathy and curiosity. She took a moment to share how she had encountered my parents while
they were on their quest for information about the elusive Sixxx bloodline. With a hint of shyness, she confessed that
the bond we shared had often drawn her to me; she had found ways to observe me when the pull of our connection became
too strong for her to ignore.

As the hours slipped by unnoticed, we suddenly became aware of the sun beginning to rise outside, casting golden rays
through the windows. I felt a twinge of anxiousness, remembering that we were vampires. But Raechelle laughed softly as
if she were reading my thoughts, her voice soothing as she explained that while the sun wouldn’t turn us to dust or
cause us harm, it would make us feel as though we were suffering from a relentless hangover if we stayed in its light
for too long. Relieved yet still playful, we decided to retreat into the comfort of sleep just after dawn. Wrapped in
each other’s arms, we succumbed to the warmth of our connection, nuzzled comfortably against the plush fabric of the
sofa, utterly content as the fire crackled softly nearby, lulling us into a peaceful slumber.

# **Chapter 5**

The warmth of the fire had dwindled to glowing embers by the time I stirred from sleep, consciousness returning in slow,
comfortable waves. A pleasant weight pressed against my chest, and I looked down to find Raechelle curled against me,
her dark hair splayed across my shoulder like a silken curtain. Her ears twitched slightly in her sleep, and her tail
was wrapped loosely around my thigh, as if anchoring herself to me even in dreams.

For a long moment, I simply lay there, marveling at how drastically my life had changed in the span of a single night.
Just yesterday, I had been an ordinary college student on a birthday trip with my parents. Now, I was orphaned, awakened
as a Blood Archon, bonded to a beautiful vampire cat familiar, and thrust into a world of magic I never knew existed.

The grief lurked at the edges of my consciousness, a dark shadow waiting to consume me if I let it. But there was
something about Raechelle's presence—the rhythmic rise and fall of her breathing, the soft warmth emanating from her
body—that kept the despair at bay. My mother had spoken of our bond, and now I understood why. Being near her felt like
coming home.

Her crimson eyes fluttered open, catching the dim light filtering through the curtains. "You're awake," she murmured,
her voice thick with sleep yet still carrying that sultry undertone that sent electricity through my veins.

"I've been watching you sleep," I admitted, reaching up to gently stroke one of her velvety ears. She made a sound
somewhere between a purr and a contented sigh, leaning into my touch.

"That's either very romantic or slightly creepy, Sir," she teased, a playful smile dancing on her lips. "I'm choosing to
believe it's the former."

"Definitely the former." I chuckled softly, the sound feeling foreign after everything that had happened. "How long were
we asleep?"

Raechelle tilted her head, her ears rotating slightly as if listening to something beyond my perception. "Based on the
quality of light outside, I'd estimate it's late afternoon. We slept through most of the day."

The reality of our situation came crashing back. My parents' bodies were still out there somewhere, in the wreckage of
the car. The thought made my stomach clench painfully.

"We need to—" I started, but Raechelle placed a gentle finger against my lips.

"I know what you're thinking," she said softly, her eyes filled with understanding. "And yes, we will need to address
your parents' remains. But there are things you need to understand first about how the magical world handles such...
incidents."

She sat up gracefully, her tail swishing behind her as she stretched with feline elegance. I couldn't help but
appreciate the way her silhouette moved in the dim light, the curves of her body accentuated by the shadows.

"The magical community has protocols for situations like this," she continued, settling cross-legged on the sofa to face
me. "There are beings whose sole purpose is to clean up supernatural incidents and ensure the mundane world remains
oblivious. By now, your parents' accident will have been staged to look like a tragic vehicle malfunction—a gas leak,
perhaps, or a tire blowout."

The clinical nature of her explanation should have disturbed me more than it did. Instead, I found myself nodding,
accepting this new reality with a detachment that surprised even me.

"And the... the ones who attacked us?" My voice hardened. "Who were they?"

Raechelle's expression darkened, her ears flattening against her head. "I didn't get a good look at them—they fled when
they sensed your awakening. But based on the method of attack, the earth spikes that..." She paused, swallowing hard.
"That took your mother. I believe they were agents of the Earth Archon."

"The Earth Archon," I repeated, the words tasting bitter on my tongue. "One of the four remaining members of the
Archonis Council?"

"Yes. His name is Terravos, and he has held his seat for nearly three centuries. He was among those who led the purge
against the Blood Mage lineages all those years ago. If he's discovered that a new Blood Archon has awakened..." She
trailed off, the implications hanging heavy in the air between us.

"Then he'll come for me."

"Yes."

The word settled into the silence like a stone dropped into still water. I should have been terrified—any sane person
would be. But instead, I felt something else stirring within me, something darker and more primal. It coiled in my chest
like a living thing, whispering promises of vengeance in a voice that sounded suspiciously like my own.
